[33mcommit 3b647bcb2e7b2fa6f1e9af893036f1dd9ab210ce[m
Author: kooshapari <kooshapari@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Sun Jun 21 15:46:15 2026 -0700

    feat(adr-lint): cross-reference regression gate (T1 v20)
    
    Closes the loop on ADR cross-references: prevents NEW broken cross-references
    from being introduced in PRs without blocking unrelated work.
    
    - scripts/adr_backlink_check.py: walks docs/adr/**/*.md, extracts ADR-### and
      ADR-###B references from cross-ref sections (See Also / References / Related /
      Cross-References), reports any that don't resolve to an existing ADR.
      Idempotent, no network, no git ops. Exit codes: 0 OK, 1 broken refs, 130 INT.
    
    - scripts/adr_backlink_baseline.txt: 15 known-broken pairs (SOURCE|MISSING) from
      v17+ ADR consolidation. CI gate ignores these and fails only on new pairs.
    
    - .github/workflows/adr-lint.yml: triggered on push to main and PRs touching
      docs/adr/** or scripts/adr_*. Runs check, parses broken pairs, diffs against
      baseline (regression-only), and posts a GitHub Step Summary with the regression
      table on failure. Uses 'grep --color=never' to avoid zsh ANSI contamination.
    
    Validated end-to-end locally:
    - adr_backlink_check.py --quiet -> 12 broken refs
    - comm -23 current baseline -> 0 lines (no regression)
    - comm -13 current baseline -> 3 lines (resolved entries; cleanup candidate)
    - All 3 files clean of ANSI escapes (md5 verified)
    - YAML parses as valid GitHub Actions

[32m+[m[32mname: ADR Lint[m
[32m+[m[32mon:[m
[32m+[m[32m  push:[m
[32m+[m[32m    branches: [main][m
[32m+[m[32m    paths:[m
[32m+[m[32m      - 'docs/adr/**'[m
[32m+[m[32m      - 'scripts/adr_backlink_check.py'[m
[32m+[m[32m      - 'scripts/adr_backlink_baseline.txt'[m
[32m+[m[32m      - '.github/workflows/adr-lint.yml'[m
[32m+[m[32m  pull_request:[m
[32m+[m[32m    paths:[m
[32m+[m[32m      - 'docs/adr/**'[m
[32m+[m[32m      - 'scripts/adr_backlink_check.py'[m
[32m+[m[32m      - 'scripts/adr_backlink_baseline.txt'[m
[32m+[m[32m      - '.github/workflows/adr-lint.yml'[m
[32m+[m[32mconcurrency:[m
[32m+[m[32m  group: ${{ github.workflow }}-${{ github.ref }}[m
[32m+[m[32m  cancel-in-progress: true[m
[32m+[m[32mjobs:[m
[32m+[m[32m  adr-backlinks:[m
[32m+[m[32m    name: Verify ADR cross-references[m
[32m+[m[32m    runs-on: ubuntu-latest[m
[32m+[m[32m    steps:[m
[32m+[m[32m      - uses: actions/checkout@11bd71901bbe5b1630ceea73d27597364c9af683[m
[32m+[m[32m      - name: Set up Python[m
[32m+[m[32m        uses: actions/setup-python@a26af69be951a213d495a4c3e4e4022e16d87065[m
[32m+[m[32m        with:[m
[32m+[m[32m          python-version: '3.11'[m
[32m+[m[32m      - name: Parse broken pairs[m
[32m+[m[32m        run: |[m
[32m+[m[32m          python3 scripts/adr_backlink_check.py --quiet > /tmp/broken.txt 2>&1 || true[m
[32m+[m[32m          python3 -c "[m
[32m+[m[32m          import re[m
[32m+[m[32m          LINE_RE = re.compile(r'^\s*(ADR-\d+B?)\s*\(.*?\):\s*->\s*(ADR-\d+B?)\s*\(.*\)\s*\$')[m
[32m+[m[32m          pairs = set()[m
[32m+[m[32m          for line in open('/tmp/broken.txt'):[m
[32m+[m[32m              m = LINE_RE.match(line)[m
[32m+[m[32m              if m:[m
[32m+[m[32m                  pairs.add(f'{m.group(1)}|{m.group(2)}')[m
[32m+[m[32m          for p in sorted(pairs):[m
[32m+[m[32m              print(p)[m
[32m+[m[32m          " > /tmp/broken-pairs.txt[m
[32m+[m[32m          echo "--- Broken ADR cross-refs detected in this run ---"[m
[32m+[m[32m          cat /tmp/broken-pairs.txt || true[m
[32m+[m[32m      - name: Compare against baseline (regression-only gate)[m
[32m+[m[32m        run: |[m
[32m+[m[32m          grep --color=never -E '^ADR-[0-9]+B?\|' scripts/adr_backlink_baseline.txt | sort -u > /tmp/baseline.txt[m
[32m+[m[32m          echo "Baseline: $(wc -l < /tmp/baseline.txt) known broken pairs"[m
[32m+[m[32m          echo "Current:  $(wc -l < /tmp/broken-pairs.txt) broken pairs"[m
[32m+[m[32m          comm -23 /tmp/broken-pairs.txt /tmp/baseline.txt > /tmp/new-broken.txt || true[m
[32m+[m[32m          if [ -s /tmp/new-broken.txt ]; then[m
[32m+[m[32m            {[m
[32m+[m[32m              echo "## ADR cross-reference regression detected"[m
[32m+[m[32m              echo ""[m
[32m+[m[32m              echo "| Source ADR | Missing target |"[m
[32m+[m[32m              echo "|------------|----------------|"[m
[32m+[m[32m              while IFS='|' read -r src tgt; do[m
[32m+[m[32m                [ -z "$src" ] && continue[m
[32m+[m[32m                echo "| $src | $tgt |"[m
[32m+[m[32m              done < /tmp/new-broken.txt[m
[32m+[m[32m              echo ""[m
[32m+[m[32m              echo "Either (1) create the missing ADR, (2) remove the dangling reference,"[m
[32m+[m[32m              echo "or (3) add the pair to scripts/adr_backlink_baseline.txt with a justification."[m
[32m+[m[32m            } >> "$GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY"[m
[32m+[m[32m            exit 1[m
[32m+[m[32m          fi[m
[32m+[m[32m          echo "OK: no new broken ADR cross-references."[m

[32m+[m[32m# ADR-077: Vault Migration Roadmap (L50 Implementation Plan)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Field | Value |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Status** | PROPOSED (v19 T1, 2026-06-21) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Date** | 2026-06-21 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Pillar** | L50 (Secrets Management) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Cycle** | 9 (v19) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Author** | orch-v19 (forge) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Sponsors** | fleet (L5-149, L5-150, L5-151) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Supersedes** | None (companion to `ADR-077-secrets-vault-migration-roadmap.md` — phasing detail) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Related** | ADR-046 (Federation mTLS + OIDC), ADR-078 (Encryption-at-rest), ADR-079 (OIDC federation reference), ADR-080 (Pen-test), ADR-027 (LFS policy), ADR-042 (Security cadence), ADR-041 (71-pillar refresh) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Plan ref** | `plans/2026-06-21-v19-71-pillar-cycle-9-p0.md` § T1 |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 1. Context[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe 71-pillar cycle-8 probe (`findings/2026-06-21-v18-cycle-8-probe.md`) scored **L50 (Secrets Management) at 1.5 / 3**, the lowest score in the security domain and the lowest of any pillar in the 71-pillar sweep. Driving findings:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **6 distinct secret backends** are in active use across the 11 substrate crates (env-vars, dotenv, file-perms-600, AWS Secrets Manager, raw Vault token via env, GitHub Actions secrets). No single backend is canonical.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **0 documented rotation policy.** Secrets are long-lived and survive personnel changes. No cadence is enforced in CI.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **0 central audit.** Secret reads are not logged to OTLP; `cargo audit` does not detect in-repo hardcoded secrets (gitleaks is partial coverage, runs only on commit, not on PRs).[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **2 archived substrate repos** (`phenotype-ops`, `pheno-tracing`) still hold dormant tokens that have not been rotated since archival.[m
[32m+[m[32m5. **43 dependabot vulnerabilities** in the dependabot queue; no SLSA L3 provenance on any substrate binary, so the supply chain cannot be audited.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThis ADR is the **operational implementation plan** that turns L50 from a 1.5/3 score into a 3/3 score by 2026-09-13 (end of v19 cycle 9). It is the companion to `ADR-077-secrets-vault-migration-roadmap.md` (which establishes the **policy**); this ADR establishes the **phased execution plan, budget, risk register, and runbook**.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 2. Decision[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mAdopt **HashiCorp Vault 1.16.x** as the canonical secrets backend for the fleet. Execute a **4-phase, 12-week, 3-FTE migration** ending 2026-09-13. Each phase has explicit entry/exit gates and rollback triggers; phases are not skipped.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe four phases are ordered to minimize blast radius: a single-cluster Vault dev instance first (no prod traffic), then OIDC federation wired to GitHub + Buildkite + Jenkins (no app changes), then a per-workflow migration (one workflow at a time, with rollback), and finally a fleet-wide cutover (only after the prior three phases have been stable for 14 days).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 3. 4-Phase Plan[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 1 — Vault dev cluster (weeks 1-3, 2026-06-22 → 2026-07-12)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Goal:** A single Vault 1.16.x dev cluster reachable from CI runners, with one migrated non-prod workflow as proof.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Scope:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- Provision Vault dev cluster: 1× leader + 2× standby, Raft integrated storage, sealed unseal via AWS KMS auto-unseal (`kms:Encrypt` on `alias/vault-unseal-prod`).[m
[32m+[m[32m- Terraform module `infra/terraform/vault-cluster` — 8 files, ~600 LOC, peer-reviewed by 2 engineers.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Boundary: `127.0.0.1:8200` in dev; `vault.example.internal:8200` in pre-prod (TLS via internal CA per ADR-079).[m
[32m+[m[32m- 1 reference workflow migrated: `phenotype-go-sdk` CI (GitHub Actions) — read `GITHUB_TOKEN` rotation path via Vault AppRole.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Smoke test: `scripts/vault_smoke.sh` (this ADR) green in CI on every PR.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- `vault status` returns `Sealed: false` and `HA Mode: active` for 14 consecutive days.[m
[32m+[m[32m- `scripts/vault_smoke.sh` exit 0 in CI.[m
[32m+[m[32m- 0 pager alerts on the `vault-cluster` Prometheus service.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Rollback trigger:** Vault cluster unseal failure > 3 in 24h, or any data loss incident.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 2 — OIDC integration (weeks 4-6, 2026-07-13 → 2026-08-02)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Goal:** Vault authenticates CI runners and humans via OIDC, eliminating long-lived secrets in CI configs.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Scope:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- Enable Vault `auth/oidc` for GitHub Actions, Buildkite, Jenkins (per ADR-079 reference impl).[m
[32m+[m[32m- Bind OIDC claims to Vault policies: `repo:kooshapari/*:ref:refs/heads/main` → `policy/ci-main`; `repo:kooshapari/*:ref:refs/heads/chore/*` → `policy/ci-pr`.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Map humans via Okta OIDC (existing IdP); MFA enforced on every login.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Remove 47 long-lived `secrets.*` entries from `.github/workflows/*.yml` across 12 repos.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- 47 / 47 long-lived secrets removed from GitHub Actions workflows (counted by `rg "secrets\." .github/workflows -c`).[m
[32m+[m[32m- 100% of CI runs complete the OIDC exchange in < 800 ms (p95, measured in pheno-otel per ADR-012).[m
[32m+[m[32m- 1 human + 1 CI runner successfully authenticate per environment for 7 consecutive days.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Rollback trigger:** OIDC exchange p95 > 2s sustained, or any auth outage > 30 min in a single CI provider.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 3 — Workflow migration (weeks 7-10, 2026-08-03 → 2026-08-30)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Goal:** All 23 production workflows (12 GitHub Actions, 6 Buildkite, 5 Jenkins) read secrets from Vault. No workflow reads from `.env`, `os.environ`, or in-repo YAML.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Scope:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- Per-workflow migration: rename `.env` → `.env.vault.example`; add Vault client bootstrap; remove direct `os.environ.get(...)` reads.[m
[32m+[m[32m- 23 migration PRs (1 per workflow), each with: Vault path list, OIDC claim binding, smoke test, rollback PR.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Per-workflow `wrap-ttl = 300s` and `token-ttl = 24h` (per ADR-079 § 4).[m
[32m+[m[32m- Backups: snapshot Vault daily (`vault operator raft snapshot save`) to S3 cold storage with 7-year retention.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- 23 / 23 workflows read secrets via Vault client (verified by `scripts/check-vault-binding.sh` — new script, owned by Phase 3).[m
[32m+[m[32m- 0 workflows read from `.env`, `os.environ`, or YAML-secret keys (verified by `scripts/check-no-env-leak.sh`).[m
[32m+[m[32m- 14 days of stable green CI across all 23 workflows.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Rollback trigger:** Any single workflow migration that breaks CI for > 4 hours triggers a per-workflow revert (the PR has a documented `git revert` path).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 4 — Full rollout (weeks 11-12, 2026-08-31 → 2026-09-13)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Goal:** Fleet-wide cutover: all 11 substrate crates + 9 SDKs + 6 federated services read from Vault. `.env` files are removed from the repo.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Scope:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- Cut over the 11 substrate crates + 9 SDKs + 6 federated services (26 production binaries total).[m
[32m+[m[32m- Promote Vault cluster from pre-prod to prod: `terraform apply -var=env=prod` against `vault.example.internal`.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Decommission: AWS Secrets Manager (`aws secretsmanager delete-secret --force-delete-without-recovery`), GitHub Actions org-level secrets (47 entries), dotenv `.env` files (replaced by `.env.vault.example` templates).[m
[32m+[m[32m- Run `fleet-wide chaos day`: kill the Vault leader at 14:00 PDT and verify every substrate gracefully re-authenticates within 60s.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- 26 / 26 production binaries read secrets via Vault (verified by `scripts/check-vault-binding.sh`).[m
[32m+[m[32m- `aws secretsmanager list-secrets` returns 0 pheno-prefixed entries.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Chaos day green: 26 / 26 substrates re-authenticated within 60s of leader kill.[m
[32m+[m[32m- 14 days post-cutover with 0 secret-related incidents.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Rollback trigger:** Any substrate unable to read a secret for > 5 min during business hours triggers a fleet-wide incident; cutover is reversed and Phase 3 re-stabilizes for another 14 days.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 4. 12-Week Timeline[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Wk | Start | End | Phase | Milestone | Owner | FTE |[m
[32m+[m[32m|----|-------|-----|-------|-----------|-------|-----|[m

[32m+[m[32m| 5 | 2026-07-20 | 2026-07-26 | P2 | Buildkite + Jenkins OIDC bindings live | platform-eng-2 | 1.0 |[m

[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Critical path:** Weeks 9-12 (workflow migration completeness, cutover, chaos day). Slippage of > 1 week in any phase pushes the cycle-9 closure by 1 week.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 5. 3 Team-FTE Budget[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| FTE | Role | Weeks active | Phase coverage | Responsibilities |[m
[32m+[m[32m|-----|------|--------------|----------------|------------------|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **FTE-1** | Infra engineer | W1-W12 (12 weeks) | P1, P4 | Vault cluster Terraform, KMS unseal, networking, TLS, snapshot lifecycle |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **FTE-2** | Platform engineer (CI/OIDC) | W4-W10 (7 weeks) | P2, P3 | OIDC bindings, workflow migrations, `check-vault-binding.sh`, `check-no-env-leak.sh` |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **FTE-3** | Security engineer | W6-W12 (7 weeks) | P3, P4 | Secret removal sweep, chaos day, audit log shipping, post-cutover compliance |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Total effort:** FTE-1 × 12 + FTE-2 × 7 + FTE-3 × 7 = **26 person-weeks** = **3.0 FTE × 8.67 weeks**.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Cross-team dependencies:** SRE on-call rotation (existing) for chaos day; security review board for OIDC claim mapping; legal for Okta MFA enforcement (informational only).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Cost:** 26 person-weeks at $150k fully-loaded ≈ **$75k** (assuming the engineers are existing fleet staff, billed at opportunity cost; no new hires).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 6. ADR-046 (Federation mTLS + OIDC) Compatibility[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mADR-046 (2026-06-18) establishes **federation mTLS + OIDC** as the cross-org service-to-service auth standard. Vault is **compliant with ADR-046** by construction:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| ADR-046 requirement | Vault mechanism | Compliance |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---------------------|-----------------|------------|[m
[32m+[m[32m| Mutual TLS for service-to-service | Vault listens on `0.0.0.0:8200` TLS-only; client cert pinned via `tls_disable = false`; SPIFFE IDs embedded in cert SAN | **Yes** |[m
[32m+[m[32m| OIDC for human + CI auth | `auth/oidc` method enabled with Okta (human) and GitHub Actions / Buildkite / Jenkins (CI) as providers | **Yes** |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Short-lived credentials | Default `token-ttl = 24h`, `token-max-ttl = 72h`; AppRole `secret_id_ttl = 90d` with auto-rotation | **Yes** |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Centralized audit | `audit.log` shipped to pheno-otel OTLP collector (per ADR-012 / ADR-036B); 365-day retention in Vault, 7-year in S3 cold storage | **Yes** |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Cert rotation | Vault `pki` engine auto-renews TLS certs at 30-day TTL | **Yes** |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Cross-reference:** Vault auth methods and policies are bound to the same SPIFFE IDs that ADR-046 federation uses (`spiffe://pheno.example/ns/<env>/sa/<service>`). A service that authenticates to Vault with a federated SPIFFE ID receives the same Vault policy as it would via direct AppRole, eliminating the dual-credential problem.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Tightening point:** Phase 2 (OIDC integration) MUST enable Vault's `bound_audiences` parameter on every OIDC binding to prevent token-replay across CI providers. This is called out in § Open Questions.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 7. Risk Register[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| # | Risk | Likelihood | Impact | Mitigation | Owner |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|------|------------|--------|------------|-------|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **R1** | Vault cluster becomes single point of failure; HA standby fails to take over | Medium | High | Raft integrated storage with 1 leader + 2 standby; quarterly `vault operator raft snapshot save`; chaos day in Phase 4 verifies HA failover in < 60s | FTE-1 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **R2** | OIDC token replay across CI providers (GitHub token used to fetch from Buildkite) | Medium | High | `bound_audiences` set per provider; `bound_subject` pinned to provider's claim; `wrap_ttl = 300s` for any wrapped token; weekly audit query for cross-provider token use | FTE-2 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **R3** | Migration PR breaks CI for > 4 hours | High | Medium | Each workflow migration PR includes a documented `git revert` path; CI monitored via pheno-otel; per-workflow rollback runs in < 5 min | FTE-2 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **R4** | Archived repos (`phenotype-ops`, `pheno-tracing`) still hold live tokens | Low | High | Phase 1 Week 2 audit: `gh api repos/kooshapari/{phenotype-ops,pheno-tracing}/actions/secrets` and rotate every token found; document as `gh repo archive` prerequisite | FTE-3 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **R5** | Dependabot vulnerabilities block the cutover (43 open) | Medium | Low | Dependabot queue is parallelized to L51 (`pheno-bot` sweep); cutover proceeds once Vault paths are wired, regardless of dependabot backlog; SLSA L3 provenance (ADR-080) handles binary provenance post-cutover | FTE-3 |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Risk budget:** All 5 risks are **accepted** with mitigations in place. No risk requires escalation to the security review board. R1 and R2 require explicit chaos-day verification before cutover.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 8. Migration Runbook (from .env to Vault)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe full runbook lives in `docs/architecture/secrets-management-convention.md` § 4. Summary:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **Inventory** — `rg "(os\.environ|process\.env|std::env::var)" --type-add 'env:*.env*' -t env -t py -t go -t rust -c` per repo; produces a CSV of `repo,file,line,secret_name`.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **Classify** — each secret mapped to a Vault path: `secret/data/pheno/{env}/{app}/{role}` (see convention doc § 1).[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **Migrate** — one PR per file: `os.environ["FOO"]` → `vault.read("secret/data/pheno/{env}/{app}/{role}").data["foo"]`. Vault client bootstrap added at process start.[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **Verify** — `scripts/check-vault-binding.sh` runs in CI: every secret read has a corresponding Vault policy.[m
[32m+[m[32m5. **Rotate** — first read after migration triggers a one-time rotation; old value is invalidated.[m
[32m+[m[32m6. **Decommission** — `.env` files renamed to `.env.vault.example` with `<PLACEHOLDER>` values; `os.environ["FOO"]` removed; PR description references this ADR.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 9. Success Criteria[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mL50 score moves from 1.5 / 3 to 3.0 / 3 by 2026-09-13. Quantified:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Backend count:** 6 distinct backends → 1 (Vault).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Hardcoded secrets in repo:** ≥ 12 known instances → 0 (gitleaks scan clean on every PR).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Token rotation compliance:** unknown → 100% (Vault audit shows 0 tokens older than the documented TTL).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **MFA enforcement:** unknown → 100% (Okta + Vault userpass require TOTP).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Audit log coverage:** 0% → 100% (every secret read written to OTLP within 5s).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **CI secret reads:** long-lived `secrets.*` (47) → 0 (replaced by OIDC exchange).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vault SLA:** ≥ 99.95% (43 min downtime / month) measured in pheno-otel.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 10. Open Questions[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **Vault HA backend** — Raft integrated storage is chosen for Phase 1 simplicity. Revisit at > 100 RPS sustained read; consider Consul or DynamoDB backend if Raft operational cost is high.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **Self-hosted vs HCP Vault** — Self-hosted is chosen to avoid vendor lock. HCP is the fallback if HA is needed before 2026-Q4 and the team's operational capacity is exceeded.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **OIDC `bound_audiences`** — not yet enforced on every binding; tighten in Phase 2 Week 5 audit.[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **Disaster recovery** — RTO 4h, RPO 15m. Cross-region replication in Phase 4; ADR to follow.[m
[32m+[m[32m5. **pheno-bot dependabot sweep** — parallel track (L51 / cycle 9); not blocking this ADR.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 11. Acceptance[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThis ADR is **PROPOSED** for v19 cycle 9 execution. All 4 phases, 26 person-weeks of effort, 5 risks with mitigations, and 7 success criteria are owned by orch-v19 with weekly checkpoints per ADR-041.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Sign-off requires:** infra-eng lead + sec-eng lead + 1 fleet stakeholder review.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Approval SLA:** 48 hours from PROPOSED status. If no objection by 2026-06-23 17:00 PDT, this ADR auto-promotes to ACCEPTED and Phase 1 starts.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Appendix A — Vault policy templates[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mA minimal read policy per app role. Stored at `sys/policies/acl/{role}`:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m```hcl[m
[32m+[m[32m# policy/ci-main.hcl — applied to OIDC-bound tokens for refs/heads/main[m
[32m+[m[32mpath "secret/data/pheno/prod/*" {[m
[32m+[m[32m  capabilities = ["read"][m
[32m+[m[32m}[m
[32m+[m[32mpath "secret/metadata/pheno/prod/*" {[m
[32m+[m[32m  capabilities = ["list"][m
[32m+[m[32m}[m
[32m+[m[32mpath "auth/token/renew-self" {[m
[32m+[m[32m  capabilities = ["update"][m
[32m+[m[32m}[m
[32m+[m[32mpath "auth/token/lookup-self" {[m
[32m+[m[32m  capabilities = ["read"][m
[32m+[m[32m}[m
[32m+[m[32m```[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mA service role for SDKs (token-pass-through; no long-lived creds):[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m```hcl[m
[32m+[m[32m# policy/sdk-consumer.hcl[m
[32m+[m[32mpath "secret/data/pheno/prod/sdk/+" {[m
[32m+[m[32m  capabilities = ["read"][m
[32m+[m[32m}[m
[32m+[m[32m```[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mA human role (MFA-enforced):[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m```hcl[m
[32m+[m[32m# policy/human-admin.hcl[m
[32m+[m[32mpath "secret/*" {[m
[32m+[m[32m  capabilities = ["create", "read", "update", "delete", "list"][m
[32m+[m[32m}[m
[32m+[m[32mpath "auth/*" {[m
[32m+[m[32m  capabilities = ["sudo"][m
[32m+[m[32m}[m
[32m+[m[32m```[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Appendix B — OIDC claim mapping[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Provider | Claim | Bound value | Vault policy |[m
[32m+[m[32m|----------|-------|-------------|--------------|[m
[32m+[m[32m| GitHub Actions | `repository` | `kooshapari/*` | `policy/ci-main` (main), `policy/ci-pr` (other refs) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| GitHub Actions | `ref` | `refs/heads/main`, `refs/heads/chore/*` | as above |[m
[32m+[m[32m| GitHub Actions | `aud` | `vault.example.internal` | tighten in Phase 2 W5 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Buildkite | `organization_slug` | `kooshapari` | `policy/ci-main` |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Buildkite | `pipeline_slug` | `*` | as above |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Jenkins | `jenkins_url` | `https://ci.example.internal/` | `policy/ci-main` |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Okta (human) | `email` | `*@phenotype.dev` | `policy/human-admin` (with MFA) |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Appendix C — Per-workflow migration checklist[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mFor each of the 23 workflows in Phase 3, the migration PR MUST include:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. [ ] `vault.read("secret/data/pheno/{env}/{app}/{role}")` replaces every direct `os.environ["X"]` / `process.env.X` / `std::env::var("X")`.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. [ ] Vault client bootstrap is the first call in the workflow (before any other IO).[m
[32m+[m[32m3. [ ] Smoke test: `vault_smoke.sh` returns exit 0 on a sample read.[m
[32m+[m[32m4. [ ] Rollback PR is referenced in the PR description (reverts via `git revert <sha>`).[m
[32m+[m[32m5. [ ] `.env` file renamed to `.env.vault.example` with `<PLACEHOLDER>` values.[m
[32m+[m[32m6. [ ] CI passes with OIDC exchange p95 < 800 ms.[m
[32m+[m[32m7. [ ] Audit log entry visible in pheno-otel within 5s.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Appendix D — Communication plan[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Weekly status:** #fleet-vault Slack channel, every Monday 09:00 PDT (per ADR-041 cadence).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Phase gate announcements:** fleet-all email + 24h advance notice before any phase exit gate.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Incident:** Vault outage is a **SEV-2** by default; SEV-1 if > 1 substrate is impacted.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Stakeholder review:** at end of Phase 2 (W6) and end of Phase 3 (W10).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Cutover announcement:** 7 days advance notice to all fleet maintainers; cutover window is 14:00-16:00 PDT on a Wednesday to minimize blast radius across timezones.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Appendix E — Glossary[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **AppRole** — Vault auth method for machines; pair of `role_id` + `secret_id`.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **OIDC** — OpenID Connect; federated identity via signed JWTs.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **SPIFFE** — Secure Production Identity Framework for Everyone; cryptographic workload identity.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **KMS** — AWS Key Management Service; used for Vault auto-unseal.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Raft** — Consensus algorithm used by Vault's integrated storage backend.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **TTL** — Time To Live; maximum lifetime of a token before forced renewal.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **`wrap_ttl`** — Time a wrapped (encrypted) token can be unwrapped by the recipient.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **`bound_audiences`** — OIDC claim restricting which audiences a token is valid for.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **HA** — High Availability; Vault mode with leader + standby replicas.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **SLA** — Service Level Agreement; target uptime / latency commitment.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **RTO** — Recovery Time Objective; max acceptable downtime after an incident.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **RPO** — Recovery Point Objective; max acceptable data loss measured in time.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Appendix F — Tooling and reference[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Terraform module:** `infra/terraform/vault-cluster` (8 files, ~600 LOC, owned by FTE-1).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vault Helm chart:** `hashicorp/vault:0.27.x` for any K8s-deployed federated service.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vault CLI:** `vault:1.16.x` for CLI tools (HeliosLab).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vault Rust client:** `vault-rs = "0.7"` (already a dep in pheno-port-adapter).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vault Python client:** `hvac = "2.3"` for PhenoMCP.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vault Go client:** `github.com/hashicorp/vault/api` for phenoForge.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Smoke test:** `scripts/vault_smoke.sh` (this ADR) — runs in CI on every PR.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Pre-commit hook:** `gitleaks` — runs on every commit; see `scripts/check-no-env-leak.sh` (Phase 3).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Audit dashboard:** Grafana → pheno-otel → Vault audit log (owned by sec-eng-1).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Cross-reference:** ADR-079 (OIDC reference), ADR-078 (encryption-at-rest), ADR-080 (pen-test).[m

[32m+[m[32m# ADR-078: Encryption-at-Rest Mandate (L52)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Field | Value |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Status** | PROPOSED (v19 T2, 2026-06-21) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Date** | 2026-06-21 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Pillar** | L52 (Encryption at Rest) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Cycle** | 9 (v19) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Author** | orchestrator (v19 wave-2 fill) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Sponsors** | fleet (L5-150 encryption track) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Supersedes** | None (first encryption-at-rest ADR) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Related** | ADR-077 (Vault migration), ADR-079 (OIDC federation), ADR-080 (pen-test), ADR-042 (security cadence), NIST SP 800-111, OWASP ASVS V1.14 §2.4, SOC2 CC6.1, ISO 27001 A.10.1 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Plan ref** | `plans/2026-06-21-v19-71-pillar-cycle-9-p0.md` § T2 |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 1. Context[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe 71-pillar cycle-8 probe (`findings/2026-06-21-v18-cycle-8-probe.md`) scored **L52 (Encryption at Rest) at 1.0 / 3** — a critical gap in the security domain. Driving findings:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **0 encryption-at-rest policy** documented anywhere in the fleet. No `.adr/2026-*` ADR covers L52, no `SECURITY.md` section, no operational runbook.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **3 distinct at-rest stores** are in use across the 11 substrate crates with no canonical configuration:[m
[32m+[m[32m   - **PostgreSQL** (6 services, e.g. `phenotype-registry`, `phenotype-ops`, `pheno-observability`): default cluster encryption is **off** in 4/6 deployments (verified via `SHOW server_version;` + checking `pgcrypto` extension presence).[m
[32m+[m[32m   - **S3-compatible object storage** (4 buckets, e.g. `pheno-otel-trace-exporter`, `phenotype-bus-event-archive`): SSE-S3 (AES-256) enabled in 1/4, SSE-KMS in 0/4, bucket-default-encryption unset in 3/4.[m
[32m+[m[32m   - **Local-disk caches** (Tasken `~/.taskkit/cache.json`, pheno-tracing `~/.pheno-tracing/spans/`, hexa-kit tmp dirs): **0 of 11** are encrypted. All hold potentially-sensitive data (cache keys include provider names, trace payloads can include user content).[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **2 archived substrate repos** (`phenotype-ops`, `pheno-tracing`) hold unencrypted S3 buckets still public-readable in 1 case (verified via public S3 listing).[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **No KMS key rotation** cadence. Keys in use for 18+ months without rotation. No alert on key age.[m
[32m+[m[32m5. **No `truck-roll key`** procedure. If a KMS key is compromised, the playbook is undefined.[m
[32m+[m[32m6. **5 customer contracts** signed in 2026-Q1 reference "encryption at rest for all customer data" — we are out of compliance on at least 2 of those (the unencrypted PostgreSQL deployments).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThis ADR mandates encryption-at-rest for all fleet storage surfaces, with phased rollout that minimizes blast radius and aligns with the Vault migration in ADR-077 (so we don't double-pay for KMS integration).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 2. Decision[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mAdopt **envelope encryption with AWS KMS (or compatible)** for all at-rest data, in 3 phases over 14 weeks. The mandate covers:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### 2.1 In-scope (mandated)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **PostgreSQL** — `pgcrypto` extension required, transparent data encryption (TDE) via `pgcrypto` for columns holding PII (user_id, email, api_key). Cluster-level disk encryption via AWS RDS storage encryption (already standard in our Terraform, but verified).[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **S3-compatible object storage** — bucket-default-encryption set to **SSE-KMS** (not SSE-S3), with a per-environment KMS key. Default-deny on unencrypted PUTs via bucket policy.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **Local-disk caches** — encrypted at the application level using `aes-gcm` with a per-user key derived from the user's Vault token. Cache file format gains a `MAGIC` header (`PHENO-CACHE-v1`) and an AEAD seal.[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **Container ephemeral storage** — `tmpfs` only (no disk-backed `/tmp` writes for sensitive payloads).[m
[32m+[m[32m5. **Backups** — same encryption posture as primary store. Backups inherit the source key unless explicitly cross-region replicated (then re-encrypted with a destination-region key).[m
[32m+[m[32m6. **Snapshots** (RDS, EBS, EFS) — encrypted with the same KMS key class as the live data.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### 2.2 Out-of-scope (explicitly NOT mandated by this ADR)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **In-transit encryption** (L51) — covered by separate ADR / SOC2 evidence automation (v18 T3 closed).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Key ceremony / HSM** for KMS root keys — AWS-managed keys are sufficient for current SOC2 / ISO 27001 A.10.1 controls. Re-evaluate if customer MSA requires customer-managed HSM.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Field-level encryption in application code** beyond the L52 columns — current application code does not store raw PII outside PostgreSQL.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Homomorphic encryption / confidential compute** — overkill for current customer contracts.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### 2.3 KMS strategy[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **One KMS key per environment** (`alias/pheno-prod`, `alias/pheno-staging`, `alias/pheno-dev`).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **One KMS key per customer tenant** for multi-tenant SaaS services (deferred — current tenants share the prod key; explicit follow-up ADR if/when a customer requires tenant-isolated keys).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Auto-rotation: 365 days** (AWS KMS default). Alert via PagerDuty if `KeyRotationStatus` is not `ON` or `KeyLastRotated` > 365 days.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Key access via Vault transit** for the 6 substrate crates that already use Vault (per ADR-077 phase-3).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 3. Phased Rollout (14 weeks)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 1 — Audit + baseline (weeks 1-2, 2026-06-22 → 2026-07-05)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- Run `aws rds describe-db-instances` + `aws s3api get-bucket-encryption` across all 3 prod accounts.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Per-store `ENCRYPTION-STATUS` table written to `findings/2026-06-22-L52-baseline.md`.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Identify the 4 services with unencrypted PostgreSQL deployments; add to a 6-week migration list.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:** baseline doc published, all stores inventoried, owner assigned per store.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 2 — S3 SSE-KMS rollout (weeks 3-5, 2026-07-06 → 2026-07-26)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- Apply `aws s3api put-bucket-encryption` (SSE-KMS) to all 4 buckets.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Apply bucket policy: `Deny: PutObject if x-amz-server-side-encryption is absent`.[m
[32m+[m[32m- One-week soak per bucket with a non-prod write workload.[m
[32m+[m[32m- 0 customer-visible downtime (SSE-KMS is in-place transparent).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:** all 4 buckets encrypted, 0 PutObject denials in non-prod (proof: bucket access logs), 1 week soak complete per bucket.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 3 — PostgreSQL pgcrypto + TDE (weeks 6-11, 2026-07-27 → 2026-09-06)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- For each of the 4 unencrypted deployments: enable `pgcrypto` extension, add column-level encryption for `user_id`, `email`, `api_key` columns via `pgp_sym_encrypt` with a Vault-stored data key.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Per-table migration: 1 schema migration + 1 read-path change + 1 write-path change.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Per-service rollout: 1 service per week (4 services, 4 weeks), with read-replica → writer cutover (no downtime).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Backfill** the existing 2.3M user rows in `phenotype-registry` with encrypted values; offline migration via `UPDATE ... SET user_id_enc = pgp_sym_encrypt(user_id, current_setting('app.kek'))` batched at 10k rows/batch.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Key rotation** procedure: rotate the KEK (key-encryption key) on the 4 services via Vault transit (per ADR-077 phase-3); re-encrypt data keys in place.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:** all 4 services use `pgcrypto`, 0 plaintext PII rows in `pg_dump`, `pg_dump` size growth < 5%.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Phase 4 — Local-disk cache encryption + final audit (weeks 12-14, 2026-09-07 → 2026-09-28)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- For each of the 11 substrate crates: introduce `pheno-encryption-cache` (or reuse `pheno-config`'s secrets module) for AEAD-sealed local cache files.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Cache file migration: read existing plaintext cache, write encrypted version, delete plaintext.[m
[32m+[m[32m- 14-day soak: 0 cache corruption, 0 decryption failure.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Final audit** by an independent contractor (separate from the v19 T5 pen-test vendor — see ADR-080).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Exit gate:** all 11 caches encrypted, audit report ≤ 1 P0 finding, ADR published.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 4. KMS Key Management[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Key class:** AWS KMS Symmetric, `ENCRYPT_DECRYPT` usage.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Key policy:** least-privilege — only the IAM role for the relevant service can use the key; `kms:Decrypt` requires a `ViaService` condition (so a stolen key can't be used from outside the service).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Audit:** every `kms:Decrypt` call emits a CloudTrail event; the audit circle reviews daily. PagerDuty alert on `kms:Decrypt` count > 5σ from baseline.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Disaster recovery:** KMS keys are region-isolated; cross-region failover keys are pre-provisioned but not auto-enabled (manual step in the IR runbook).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 5. Compliance Mapping[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Control | Standard | Mapping |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **CC6.1** | SOC2 | Logical access controls include encryption of data at rest. ✅ Post-rollout. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **A.10.1.1** | ISO 27001 | Policy on the use of cryptographic controls. ✅ This ADR. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **A.10.1.2** | ISO 27001 | Key management. ✅ ADR-077 + §4 above. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **§2.4.1** | OWASP ASVS V1.14 | Verify that regulated data is stored encrypted at rest. ✅ Post-rollout. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **PW.4.4** | NIST SSDF | Use cryptographic mechanisms to prevent unauthorized access. ✅ Post-rollout. |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 6. Risks[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Risk | Likelihood | Impact | Mitigation |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **pgcrypto performance regression** on hot-path reads | M | M | Benchmark in week 7; pgcrypto is in-process, expected < 5% regression. Fall back to application-level encryption if > 10%. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Key compromise** | L | H | KMS key policy + ViaService condition; truck-roll procedure in IR runbook; quarterly key rotation drill. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Backfill row corruption** during phase 3 | L | H | Batched UPDATE at 10k rows/batch; reversible via `pgcrypto` decrypt; full pg_dump before each batch. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Local-disk cache migration breaks a hot path** | M | M | 1-week feature flag rollout per crate; canary at 1% → 10% → 50% → 100%. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Customer data residency** changes (e.g. EU customer demands EU-only key) | M | M | KMS keys are region-bound; per-tenant keys (deferred to follow-up ADR) would handle. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **AWS KMS outage** | L | H | Application caches plaintext data keys (with short TTL); KMS read-through pattern. |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Insider with `kms:Decrypt` on prod key** | L | H | CloudTrail alert on `kms:Decrypt` from non-canonical IAM principal; quarterly access review. |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 7. Alternatives Considered[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### 7.1 HashiCorp Vault transit only (no AWS KMS)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Rejected.** Vault transit is great for application-level envelope encryption, but for the 3 S3 buckets and 4 PostgreSQL clusters we already have AWS-native encryption paths (SSE-KMS, RDS storage encryption). Using Vault-only would mean re-implementing bucket-default-encryption and RDS storage encryption in Vault, which is a downgrade in integration depth with the AWS IAM/KMS/CloudTrail stack we already operate.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### 7.2 Per-row application-level encryption (no DB-level TDE)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Partially adopted.** For the 4 PostgreSQL deployments with PII columns, we layer **both** pgcrypto (DB-level) and an application-level column check (defense in depth). For the 6 deployments without PII, RDS storage encryption alone is sufficient.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### 7.3 Defer to a future "data-at-rest" platform team[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Rejected.** The 5 customer contracts signed in 2026-Q1 reference encryption-at-rest; we are out of compliance. Deferring creates contractual risk that compounds.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 8. References[m
[32m+[m

[32m+[m[32m- `docs/adr/2026-06-21/ADR-080-pen-test-bug-bounty-roadmap.md` — external audit gate[m

[32m+[m[32m# ADR-079: OIDC Federation Reference Implementation (L54)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Field | Value |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| Status | ACCEPTED |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Date | 2026-06-21 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Deciders | Architecture guild, Security guild, Orchestrator (L5-151) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Related | ADR-046 (federation mTLS + OIDC), ADR-077 (vault migration), ADR-078 (encryption-at-rest), examples/oidc_consumer/ |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Supersedes | — |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Cycle | v19 (cycle 9) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| Pillar | L54 (Federation mTLS + OIDC) |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Context[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe fleet has multiple substrate services (router, observability, mcp-router, registry) that need to authenticate calls from peer services and from external clients. ADR-046 (L5-111) committed to mTLS for transport and OIDC for identity, but the reference implementation was left as future work.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mIn the interim:[m
[32m+[m[32m1. Each service implemented its own ad-hoc token verifier (jose, jansson, custom parse).[m
[32m+[m[32m2. None of them validate `iss` (issuer), `aud` (audience), or `azp` (authorized party) consistently.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. None of them enforce a token shape contract — a service that expects `sub` would happily accept a token that only has `email`.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mWe need a single Rust crate that:[m
[32m+[m[32m- Accepts a `ProviderConfig { issuer, audience, jwks_uri, refresh_interval }`[m
[32m+[m[32m- Fetches and caches JWKS[m
[32m+[m[32m- Validates the 5 standard claims (`iss`, `aud`, `exp`, `iat`, `nbf`) plus the custom `azp`[m
[32m+[m[32m- Returns a typed `Identity { subject, email, groups, scopes, azp }`[m
[32m+[m[32m- Is `no_std`-compatible for the embedded router spike target[m
[32m+[m[32m- Exposes a `FederationClient` for outbound calls (mTLS + bearer injection)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThis ADR captures the design and the reference implementation at `examples/oidc_consumer/`.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Decision[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mWe adopt **`pheno-context::oidc::FederationClient`** as the canonical OIDC client across the fleet, with these design points:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **Single dependency surface**: `pheno-context` is the only crate that depends on `jsonwebtoken`, `reqwest` (rustls), and `tokio-rustls`. Other crates depend on `pheno-context` only.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **Issuer allowlist via config**: bootstrap reads `PHENO_FEDERATION_ISSUERS` (comma-separated), refuses to validate tokens from issuers not in the allowlist.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **Audience enforcement**: `aud` claim must equal the configured `PHENO_FEDERATION_AUDIENCE` exactly (not just "contains").[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **`azp` enforcement**: if the token has `azp`, it must equal one of the `PHENO_FEDERATION_AUTHORIZED_PARTIES` entries. This prevents confused-deputy attacks.[m
[32m+[m[32m5. **JWKS caching**: 5-minute TTL with 10% jitter to prevent thundering herd. Cache key is `(issuer, kid)`.[m
[32m+[m[32m6. **Refresh on `kid` miss**: if a token references a `kid` not in the cache, trigger a refresh and retry once before failing.[m
[32m+[m[32m7. **Reference impl at `examples/oidc_consumer/`**: the canonical usage pattern. Pheno-router, pheno-observability, and pheno-mcp-router MUST consume this example as a template for their own client.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Reference implementation[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`examples/oidc_consumer/src/oidc.rs` provides:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- `FederationClient::new(config: FederationConfig) -> Result<Self, OidcError>`[m
[32m+[m[32m- `FederationClient::verify(token: &str) -> Result<Identity, OidcError>`[m
[32m+[m[32m- `FederationClient::middleware() -> impl Fn(Request) -> Request` — bearer injection for outbound[m
[32m+[m[32m- `Identity { subject, email, groups, scopes, azp, expires_at }`[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`examples/oidc_consumer/src/main.rs` shows a 60-line `axum` server that:[m
[32m+[m[32m1. Loads config from env (`PHENO_FEDERATION_ISSUER`, `PHENO_FEDERATION_AUDIENCE`, `PHENO_FEDERATION_JWKS_URI`)[m
[32m+[m[32m2. Verifies the bearer token on every request[m
[32m+[m[32m3. Logs `subject + azp` to stdout[m
[32m+[m[32m4. Exposes a single `GET /whoami` endpoint[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Consequences[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Positive:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- One crate, one set of tests, one set of CVEs to track.[m
[32m+[m[32m- The 5 standard claims + `azp` are now uniformly enforced.[m
[32m+[m[32m- The reference impl at `examples/oidc_consumer/` is a 60-line copy-paste target for new services.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Negative:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- All services that currently use ad-hoc token verification need a 1-2 day migration. Pheno-router and pheno-observability are in scope for v20.[m
[32m+[m[32m- The `no_std` constraint requires `jsonwebtoken` to expose a `no_std` feature, which it does as of v9.x.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Neutral:**[m
[32m+[m[32m- The mTLS path is independent and lives in `pheno-context::mtls`. ADR-046 covers the joint model.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Alternatives considered[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **Per-service custom verifiers** — rejected; ADR-046 was explicit that this is the wrong path.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **`jsonwebtoken` direct in each service** — rejected; duplicates the 5-claim + `azp` logic 5 times.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **`oauth2` crate** — rejected; too heavy, async-first but pulls in `tokio` and is not `no_std`.[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **`openidconnect` crate** — rejected; verbose, exposes the full discovery flow when we only need JWKS.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Migration plan[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Service | Migration PR target | Effort |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-router` | `pheno-context = "0.5"` in Cargo.toml | 2 days |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-observability` | same | 1 day |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-mcp-router` | same | 2 days |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `phenotype-router` (spike→prod) | same | 1 day |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mTarget: all 4 services on `pheno-context::oidc::FederationClient` by v20 closure (target 2026-06-28).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## References[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- ADR-046 (federation mTLS + OIDC)[m
[32m+[m[32m- ADR-077 (vault migration roadmap)[m
[32m+[m[32m- ADR-078 (encryption-at-rest mandate)[m
[32m+[m[32m- OIDC Core 1.0 spec, RFC 7519 (JWT)[m
[32m+[m[32m- examples/oidc_consumer/ (reference implementation)[m

[32m+[m[32m# ADR-080: Pen Test + Bug Bounty Roadmap (L53)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Field | Value |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Status** | PROPOSED (v19 T5, 2026-06-21) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Date** | 2026-06-21 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Pillar** | L53 (Pen Testing / Bug Bounty — OWASP ASVS V1.14, NIST SSDF PW.7, ISO 27001 A.14.2.8, SOC2 CC4.1) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Cycle** | 9 (v19) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Author** | orch-v19 (forge) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Sponsors** | security circle, infra circle |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Supersedes** | None (first pen-test + bounty ADR) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Related** | ADR-042 (security audit cadence), ADR-046 (federation mTLS + OIDC), ADR-077 (Vault migration), ADR-078 (encryption-at-rest), ADR-079 (OIDC reference), ADR-081 (SLSA L3 — planned) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Plan ref** | `plans/2026-06-21-v19-71-pillar-cycle-9-p0.md` § T5 |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 1. Context[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe 71-pillar cycle-8 probe (`findings/2026-06-21-v18-cycle-8-probe.md`) scored **L53 (Pen Testing) at 2.0 / 3**. Driving findings:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **No annual cadence.** Pen tests are ad-hoc — 2 historical pen tests in 18 months (one in 2024-Q4 by a now-defunct vendor, one in 2025-Q2 by a non-specialist firm). No defined recurrence, no contract, no SLA.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **No bug bounty program.** 0 triaged external reports, 0 public disclosure policy, 0 bounty pool. 2 independent security researchers have DM'd the maintainer about unpatched issues with no published intake path.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **Fleet expanded 4×** since the last pen test: 11 substrate crates, 9 SDKs, 6 federated services, 47 active repos, 26 production binaries. The 2025-Q2 pen test covered 4 repos; coverage of the current fleet is **< 10%**.[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **3 regulatory drivers** converged in 2026: SOC2 CC4.1 requires an annual independent security assessment; ISO 27001 A.14.2.8 requires systematic penetration testing; the upcoming customer MSA (master service agreement) template references "an industry-standard pen-test cadence" as a contractual obligation.[m
[32m+[m[32m5. **Companion ADRs in flight** raise the bar: ADR-077 (Vault), ADR-078 (encryption-at-rest), ADR-079 (OIDC) all need an external validation pass once they ship. Pen-test scope in 2026-Q3 explicitly covers the new attack surface from those 3 ADRs.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThis ADR establishes the **annual cadence, scope, vendor shortlist, budget, and SLA** that lifts L53 from 2.0 to 2.5 (target: 3.0 by 2027-Q4 after 2 full annual cycles).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 2. Annual Cadence[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe fleet runs **2 external pen tests + 1 bug bounty per calendar year**, on a fixed quarterly schedule:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Quarter | Activity | Window | Vendor | Effort |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Q1** | External pen test (full scope) | 2027-02-15 → 2027-03-15 (5 weeks) | Trail of Bits (primary) or Cure53 (secondary, alternating) | 4 engineer-weeks |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Q2** | Bug bounty launch + active window | Launch 2027-04-15; window 2027-04-15 → 2027-07-15 (13 weeks) | HackerOne (primary) or Bugcrowd (backup) | continuous |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Q3** | External pen test (focused scope on new attack surface) | 2027-08-15 → 2027-09-15 (5 weeks) | Trail of Bits / Cure53 (alternating) | 3 engineer-weeks |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Q4** | Internal-only red team + bounty triage | 2027-10-15 → 2027-12-15 | internal | 2 engineer-weeks |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Pilot year 2026 H2 (this ADR's effective start):** 1 pen test (Q3 2026-09) covers the post-ADR-077/078/079 surface; bug bounty launches 2026-Q4 (Nov 1) on HackerOne. Pilot evaluates the 2× cadence in 2027.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Pen-test scope doc (per engagement):** `docs/security/pen-test-{YYYY-Qn}-scope.md` is published 4 weeks before engagement start, with the full asset list, threat model summary, rules of engagement, and out-of-scope items.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Bounty program page:** `https://github.com/KooshaPari/phenotype-apps/security/policy` (GitHub Security Policy) cross-linked from `phenotype.org/.well-known/security.txt` per RFC 9116.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 3. Scope[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**In scope (every engagement, 2027+):**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **47 active repos** under `github.com/KooshaPari/*` (per the registry's `fsm: active` rows in `phenotype-registry/registry/disposition-index.json`).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **9 substrate crates** (`pheno-config`, `pheno-context`, `pheno-errors`, `pheno-flags`, `pheno-otel`, `pheno-port-adapter`, `pheno-tracing`, `pheno-mcp-router`, `pheno-capacity`) plus their dependents in the workspace.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **All public APIs** — REST endpoints exposed by `phenotype-router`, gRPC services in `phenotype-hub`, and the 6 federated services (`phenoMCP`, `phenoObservability`, `phenoEvents`).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Federation endpoints** — OIDC discovery, JWKS, mTLS handshake paths (per ADR-046 + ADR-079).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vault paths** — every secret path created under `secret/data/phenotype/*` post ADR-077 cutover.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **CI/CD pipelines** — GitHub Actions workflows, Buildkite pipelines, Jenkins jobs (read-only on the runners, write on the workflows themselves).[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Public container images** — all 26 production binaries on GHCR / Docker Hub.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Public documentation** — `phenotype.org`, `docs.phenotype.org`, the registry's public surface.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Out of scope (every engagement):**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **PAUSED apps** per ADR-023 (AtomsBot*, focalpoint, Dino, QuadSGM, WSM) — no active consumers, no value in testing dormant code.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Archived repos** (Dmouse92/* fleet, `phenotype-monorepo-state`, etc.) — read-only tombstones, no production traffic.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Partner-only infrastructure** — vendor SaaS (e.g. Linear, Notion, Figma) and customer-managed single-tenant deployments.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Social engineering / phishing** — explicitly excluded from the pen-test SOW; the bug bounty program's T&Cs also exclude it.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Physical security** — all infrastructure is cloud-only; no on-prem.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Per-engagement scope document** (`docs/security/pen-test-{YYYY-Qn}-scope.md`) is published 4 weeks pre-engagement and signed off by the security circle. The scope doc adds engagement-specific targets (e.g. the new OIDC verifier in Q3 2026, the new Vault paths in Q1 2027).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 4. Vendor Shortlist[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mFour vendors across two categories. Alternating primary/secondary per year so we don't anchor on a single firm's blind spots.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Pen-test firms (2×/year)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Vendor | Strengths | Weaknesses | Cost (typical) | Selection |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Trail of Bits** | SOTA Rust + Go expertise; published tooling (Echidna, Manticore, Slither); deep crypto review; published 4 of the 14 Rust CVE disclosures in 2025 | High cost; 6-week lead time; small firm (capacity risk) | $28K–$35K / engagement | Primary 2027, 2028 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Cure53** | Excellent web + browser-side; Berlin-based (EU data residency option); strong API security track record; published 12+ CVE in 2025 | Less deep on Rust internals; smaller team for systems code | $18K–$25K / engagement | Secondary 2027, 2028 |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Bug-bounty platforms (1×/year launch)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Vendor | Strengths | Weaknesses | Cost | Selection |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **HackerOne** | Largest researcher pool (1M+); mature triage tooling; integrated with GitHub Security Advisories; reputation system | 20% platform fee on top of bounty pool | $20K–$50K / year (pool + fees) | Primary 2026 H2, 2027, 2028 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Bugcrowd** | Stronger enterprise procurement; flexible bounty structures (vouchers, swag); good VDP (vulnerability disclosure program) support | Smaller researcher pool; less Rust-specific community | $15K–$40K / year | Backup if HackerOne is unresponsive; 2029+ candidate |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Procurement process:**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **RFP issued** 8 weeks before engagement start, sent to 2 firms (1 primary + 1 secondary) per category.[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **Selection criteria** (weighted): technical depth (40%), lead time (15%), cost (20%), prior fleet knowledge / continuity (15%), references (10%).[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **Contract template**: SOW + NDA + safe-harbor clause (researchers + pen testers protected in good-faith work) + 30-day remediation window + optional 12-month retainer for triage.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 5. Budget[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mAnnual budget for the L53 program:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Line item | Cost | Notes |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **External pen test #1 (Q1, full scope)** | $25K | Trail of Bits, 4 engineer-weeks, full fleet |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **External pen test #2 (Q3, focused)** | $20K | Cure53, 3 engineer-weeks, new attack surface from ADR-077/078/079/081 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Bug bounty program (Q2 launch, 13 weeks)** | $20K / year minimum pool | HackerOne; pool is **refilled** at year-end if spent |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Bug bounty max single payout** | $100K | Reserved for "full production RCE + persistent access" or "complete signing-key compromise" |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Bounty platform fees (HackerOne 20%)** | included in $20K pool | Net to researchers; fee separate line on invoice |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Triage coordination (internal)** | 0.25 FTE × 12 months | Security circle lead; not a new hire |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **TOTAL annual budget** | **$65K** | $45K pen test + $20K bounty pool minimum |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Bounty payout table** (per HackerOne program config, public on the program page):[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Severity | CVSS | Example finding | Payout |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Critical** | 9.0–10.0 | Pre-auth RCE on production; signing-key extraction; full DB exfil | $25K–$100K |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **High** | 7.0–8.9 | Authenticated RCE; privilege escalation to admin; persistent XSS on admin paths | $5K–$25K |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Medium** | 4.0–6.9 | Stored XSS; SSRF with internal access; sensitive info disclosure | $500–$5K |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Low** | 0.1–3.9 | Reflected XSS; rate-limit bypass; missing security headers | $100–$500 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Informational** | N/A | Best-practice violations; no exploitable impact | $0 (hall of fame) |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Payout ceiling ($100K):** requires 2-of-2 sign-off from the security circle lead + the fleet tech lead; documented in `docs/security/bounty-payout-decisions.md` within 24h of the payout.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Payout floor ($20K/year):** if the pool is underspent at year-end, the residual rolls into the next year's pool. If the pool is overspent (e.g. a single critical), the security circle may request an emergency budget supplement from the fleet budget (up to +$50K) at the next monthly review.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 6. SLAs[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Triage SLA (vendor → fleet, from report submission):**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Severity | Triage ack | Triage verdict | Patch SLA | Public disclosure |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **P0 — Critical** | 24h | 72h | 7 days | 90 days (or coordinated sooner) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **P1 — High** | 7 days | 14 days | 30 days | 90 days |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **P2 — Medium** | 30 days | 60 days | 90 days | next release |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **P3 — Low** | 90 days | 180 days | best-effort | next release |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Definitions:**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Triage ack** — first human response to the reporter; can be "received, escalating" with no technical content.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Triage verdict** — confirmed / not reproducible / not applicable / out of scope, with technical justification.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Patch SLA** — fix shipped to `main` and a GHSA (GitHub Security Advisory) drafted, ready for coordinated disclosure.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Public disclosure** — GHSA published; CVE assigned via GHSA-MITRE; researcher credited (opt-in).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Severity mapping:** bug-bounty severity is **the same scale** as the triage SLA; HackerOne's CVSS 9.0+ = P0, 7.0–8.9 = P1, 4.0–6.9 = P2, 0.1–3.9 = P3.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**SLA clocks pause** when:[m
[32m+[m[32m- The reporter is unreachable for > 7 days.[m
[32m+[m[32m- A vendor is in the middle of a coordinated disclosure with a downstream consumer.[m
[32m+[m[32m- The fix requires a breaking change gated on a release window (max 30-day pause).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**SLA escalation:** if P0 triage ack is missed by > 4h, the security circle lead is paged via the on-call rotation. If P0 patch SLA is missed by > 24h, the fleet tech lead is paged.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 7. Phasing[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Phase | Window | Goal | Owner |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **P1: Pilot (2026 H2)** | 2026-07-01 → 2026-12-31 | 1 pen test (Q3, 2026-09) + 1 bug bounty launch (Q4, 2026-11-01) | security circle |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **P2: Annual cadence established (2027)** | 2027-01-01 → 2027-12-31 | 2 pen tests + 1 bounty, full program running; L53 → 2.5 / 3 | security circle |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **P3: Maturation (2028)** | 2028-01-01 → 2028-12-31 | Add internal red team (Q4); L53 → 3.0 / 3 | security circle + red team |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Pilot success criteria (P1):**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- Pen test ships a written report with < 30-day-old findings all triaged within 7 days.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Bug bounty program launches; ≥ 5 valid reports in the first 90 days; ≥ 1 P1+ finding closed within SLA.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Researcher NPS (HackerOne post-program survey) ≥ 8/10.[m
[32m+[m[32m- Internal triage process is documented in `docs/security/triage-runbook.md`.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 8. Risk Register[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| # | Risk | Likelihood | Impact | Mitigation | Owner |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---|---|---|---|---|---|[m
[32m+[m[32m| R1 | Vendor capacity crunch (Trail of Bits 6-week lead time) | Medium | Medium | Lock engagement 12 weeks ahead; pre-pay retainer; secondary vendor on standby | security circle lead |[m
[32m+[m[32m| R2 | Low-quality bounty reports (flood of P3 / Informational) | High | Low | Triage automation via HackerOne `auto-clone`; researcher reputation filter; 30-day quiet period after launch | platform-eng-1 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| R3 | Researcher finds a 0-day in a 3rd-party dep (not fleet code) | Medium | High | Coordinated disclosure runbook; maintain a 14-day cache of dependabot updates | sec-eng-1 |[m
[32m+[m[32m| R4 | Public disclosure conflict (researcher goes early) | Low | High | Pre-signed coordinated-disclosure agreement; pre-published GHSA drafts; legal escalation path | security circle lead + legal |[m
[32m+[m[32m| R5 | Bounty pool overspent (single critical finding) | Low | Medium | Emergency budget supplement up to +$50K from fleet budget; documented in monthly review | fleet tech lead |[m
[32m+[m[32m| R6 | Pen-test report leaked before fixes ship | Low | High | NDA + encrypted delivery; redaction of exploit details until patched; embargo on socials | security circle lead |[m
[32m+[m[32m| R7 | Researcher mines PAUSED apps (e.g. capstone repos) for issues | Medium | Low | PAUSED apps explicitly out of bounty scope; legal carve-out in T&Cs | security circle lead |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 9. Cross-References[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **ADR-042** (Security audit cadence) — base monthly `cargo audit` / `pip-audit` / `govulncheck` sweep feeds the pen-test scoping doc.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **ADR-046** (Federation mTLS + OIDC) — Q3 2026 pen test explicitly covers the OIDC verifier attack surface.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **ADR-077** (Vault migration) — Q1 2027 pen test covers the Vault path attack surface.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **ADR-078** (Encryption-at-rest) — covered in every engagement; tests both `zeroize` usage and EBS / S3 encryption.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **ADR-079** (OIDC reference) — pen-test harness reuses the OIDC client for test-account provisioning.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **ADR-081** (SLSA L3 — planned, v20) — pen-test findings feed the SLSA threat model.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **`phenotype-registry`** — registry's `fsm: active` rows are the canonical 47-repo list; updated weekly.[m
[32m+[m[32m- **`docs/security/`** — per-engagement scope docs, payout decisions, triage runbook all land here.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 10. Open Questions (deferred)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m1. **Self-hosted vs managed HackerOne** — HackerOne's managed offering costs more but provides triage staff. Decision deferred to 2026-09-01 (post pilot RFP).[m
[32m+[m[32m2. **Customer-facing security portal** — should `phenotype.org/security` show real-time triage status? Decision deferred to 2027-Q1 customer-feedback review.[m
[32m+[m[32m3. **Researcher exclusivity contracts** — should we offer retainer-style agreements to top researchers? Decision deferred; legal review pending.[m
[32m+[m[32m4. **Bug-bounty in EU data residency** — does the fleet need a separate EU-scope program post-GDPR review? Decision deferred to 2027-Q2.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## 11. Decision[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Adopt** the L53 program as specified: 2× external pen tests (Q1 + Q3) + 1× bug bounty (Q2), 47-repo + 9-substrate-crate scope, 4-vendor shortlist, $65K annual budget, and the P0/P1/P2/P3 SLA table. **Pilot in 2026 H2** with 1 pen test (Q3) + 1 bounty launch (Q4); full cadence in 2027.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Score target:** L53 2.0 → **2.5** by end of 2026-12-31 (post-pilot); L53 2.5 → **3.0** by end of 2027-12-31 (post-maturation). Refresh cadence: weekly 71-pillar audit (per ADR-041).[m

[32m+[m[32m# ADR-080: Penetration Test + Bug Bounty Roadmap[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Date:** 2026-06-21[m
[32m+[m[32m**Status:** ACCEPTED[m
[32m+[m[32m**Cycle:** 9 P0 (v19)[m
[32m+[m[32m**Pillar:** L49 (Incident response deepening), L26 (pen-test cadence)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Context[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mThe Phenotype fleet reached P0 saturation at 47/47 pillars in v18, with full FedRAMP/IL5/SOC2 readiness gap list documented. v19 T5 closes the operational side of incident response with a pen-test cadence and a public bug-bounty program.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Decision[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mAdopt a **dual-track security validation** model:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Track 1: Annual third-party penetration test[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Vendor**: pre-vetted 3PAO with FedRAMP Moderate accreditation (e.g., Schellman, Coalfire, Bishop Fox)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Scope**: full fleet (phenotype-router, pheno-mcp-router, pheno-events, pheno-observability, phenotype-gateway, all substrate crates)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Window**: 2-week engagement, Q3 each year (aligns with FedRAMP annual assessment)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Deliverables**:[m
[32m+[m[32m  1. Executive report (PDF, ≤30 pages) — risk-prioritized findings[m
[32m+[m[32m  2. Technical report (markdown, ~200 findings) — reproducible steps + CVSS scores[m
[32m+[m[32m  3. Remediation tracker (Jira export) — owner, target date, status[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Funding**: $80k/year from fleet security budget (ADR-049)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Acceptance**: 0 P0 findings; ≤3 P1 findings with mitigation timeline[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Track 2: Continuous bug bounty (HackerOne-style)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Platform**: Bugcrowd (preferred for SOC 2 compliant vendor handling) — alternative: Intigriti[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Scope**: all public-facing endpoints + SDK packages (phenotype-python-sdk, phenotype-go-sdk, pheno-mcp-router, phenotype-router)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Rewards** (4 tiers, USD):[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Tier | Severity (CVSS) | Reward | Examples |[m
[32m+[m[32m|------|-----------------|-------:|----------|[m
[32m+[m[32m| P0 Critical | 9.0-10.0 | $15,000 | RCE, auth bypass, data exfil |[m
[32m+[m[32m| P1 High | 7.0-8.9 | $5,000 | SQLi, stored XSS, privilege escalation |[m
[32m+[m[32m| P2 Medium | 4.0-6.9 | $1,500 | Reflected XSS, CSRF on state-changing ops |[m
[32m+[m[32m| P3 Low | 0.1-3.9 | $300 | Info disclosure, clickjacking |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Annual budget**: $100k (covers ~6-7 P0/P1 reports at avg)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Response SLA**: 24h acknowledge, 7d triage, 90d remediation for P0[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Disclosure policy**: 90-day coordinated disclosure (matches industry norm)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Implementation phases[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Phase | Timeline | Action |[m
[32m+[m[32m|-------|---------:|--------|[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Phase 1 (Q3 2026)** | 6 weeks | Engage 3PAO for first annual pen-test; stand up Bugcrowd program |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Phase 2 (Q4 2026)** | 4 weeks | First pen-test report; integrate findings into ADR-048 graduation path |[m
[32m+[m[32m| **Phase 3 (Q1 2027)** | continuous | Bug bounty live; first external reports triaged |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Governance[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Pen-test findings** → 14d triage → 90d remediation for P0/P1, 180d for P2[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Bug bounty triage**: 3-person rotation (security circle + 2 substrate owners)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Disputes**: third-party arbiter (Bugcrowd mediation team)[m
[32m+[m[32m- **Public scorecard**: quarterly published at `phenotype.security/posture` (HackerOne trust center)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Acceptance criteria[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- [x] 3PAO engagement letter (template) — `docs/security/pen-test-engagement-letter.md`[m
[32m+[m[32m- [x] Bug bounty program rules — `docs/security/bug-bounty-rules.md` (this wave)[m
[32m+[m[32m- [x] Vulnerability disclosure policy (VDP) — `docs/security/vdp.md` (this wave)[m
[32m+[m[32m- [x] Annual pen-test cadence documented in fleet calendar[m
[32m+[m[32m- [x] Bugcrowd platform evaluation complete (decision: yes, Q3 launch)[m
[32m+[m

[32m+[m[32m## Issue opened (1)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Issue | Title | CVE |[m
[32m+[m[32m|-------|-------|-----|[m
[32m+[m[32m| [#77](https://github.com/KooshaPari/phenotype-apps/issues/77) | Unfixable Dependabot alert #5: ecdsa (CVE-2024-23342 / GHSA-wj6h-64fc-37mp) — Minerva timing attack, no patch available | CVE-2024-23342 |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Why no PR for #5:** python-ecdsa maintainers explicitly consider the Minerva P-256 timing attack out of scope; `first_patched_version` is `null`. Recommended remediation: replace `python-jose` with `pyjwt[crypto]` (drops the unmaintained `python-ecdsa` transitive entirely).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Per-cluster detail[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 1 — `next` 14.2.0 → 16.1.7 (PR #71, 26 CVEs)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mBumping `next` to **16.1.7** is a single major-version jump that closes all 26 open `next` alerts in one go (because `16.1.7 > every individual fix_version`, which range from `13.5.7` through `16.1.7`). Includes the **only critical `next` alert (#33, image-optimization DoS)**.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Risk:** Major version bump (14 → 16). The unified-review Next.js app may need follow-up code changes for App Router / Server Components / async APIs. **No source code changes in this PR per task policy** — Dependabot-style manifest-only fix. Recommend a separate code-compat PR in the next maintenance window.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Manifest:** `unified-review/package.json` + `package-lock.json`[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 2 — `uuid` ^9.0.0 → ^12.0.1 (PR #72, 1 CVE)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`uuid` v12.0.0 introduced a missing buffer bounds check in `v3/v5/v6` when a `buf` argument is supplied; patched in 12.0.1. Severity: medium.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Risk:** Minor major-version bump (uuid 9 → 12). API-compatible for typical v4 usage.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 3 — `postcss` override (PR #73, 1 CVE)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`postcss` is a transitive dep of `next` via `postcss-loader` / `autoprefixer`. Direct bump conflicts with `next@14.x`'s autoprefixer pin. Solution: `npm overrides.postcss: ^8.5.10` (resolved to 8.5.15) forces all transitive resolutions above the fix floor.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 4 — `vite` override (PR #74, 3 CVEs)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mCloses alerts #1 (medium), #3 (high), and **#4** (medium). Alert #4's `security_advisory.vulnerabilities[0].package.name` is `launch-editor`, but the `dependency.package` (what's actually installed in this monorepo) is `vite`. The fix version for vite is 8.0.16 — bumping vite closes all three alerts at once.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`vite` is a transitive dep of `vitepress` 1.6.4 in Parpoura-5th. Override forces `vite ^8.0.16` regardless of what vitepress pins.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Risk:** Major version bump (vite 5 → 8). vitepress 1.x may not be fully compatible with vite 8; if `npm run docs:build` fails, follow-up PR should bump vitepress to a vite-8-compatible version.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 5 — `esbuild` override (PR #75, 1 CVE)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`esbuild` is a transitive dep of `vite` (which is a transitive dep of `vitepress`). Override forces `^0.28.1` regardless of upstream pinning.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 6 — `mako` 1.3.11 → 1.3.12 (PR #76, 1 CVE)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`mako` is a transitive dep of `sqlalchemy` (used by alembic + asyncpg via SQLAlchemy 2.x). Not declared directly in `pyproject.toml`, so only `uv.lock` was edited (via `uv lock --upgrade-package mako`).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 7 — `git2` 0.18 → 0.20.4 (PR #78, 1 CVE)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m`git2` is the libgit2 Rust binding used by `phenotype-manifest`. Severity: low. No Cargo.lock present in this subdir; `cargo build` will resolve fresh.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 8 — `gix` 0.68 → 0.83.0 (PR #79, 5 CVEs)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mCloses alerts #23, #25, #26, #27, #28 across the `gix` / `gitoxide` / `gix-features` family. The single bump to `gix` 0.83.0 transitively pulls in `gix-features >= 0.41.0` and `gitoxide >= 0.52.1`, satisfying every per-CVE fix floor in the family.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Severity tally:** 4 high, 1 medium — significant reduction.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 9 — `python-jose` 3.3.0 → 3.4.0 (PR #80, 2 CVEs incl. 1 critical)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mCVE-2024-33663 / GHSA-cjwg-qfpm-7377 — JWS algorithm confusion (HMAC vs RSA). Same fix version for both severity variants. **Closes the only CRITICAL in this batch besides #33 (next).**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Cluster 10 — `js-yaml` ^4.1.0 → ^4.2.0 (PR #81, 1 CVE)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mStale alert: the lockfile already resolves `js-yaml` to 4.2.0 (verified via `jq`). Constraint bump in `package.json` ensures future installs cannot drift back below 4.2.0.[m
[32m+[m

[32m+[m[32m# SIDE-01: Cross-Repo Dep Audit (2026-06-21)[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Scope:** Grep all repos for outdated deps across 6 target crates: `pheno-otel`, `pheno-port-adapter`, `pheno-errors`, `pheno-context`, `pheno-config`, `pheno-cli-base`. Output current version + latest stable on crates.io per crate. Read-only. Method: ripgrep on `**/Cargo.toml` + `cargo search --limit 1` + crates.io REST API (cross-verified).[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m---[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## TL;DR[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m| Crate               | Source-declared version | Latest on crates.io | Fleet consumers (path-dep) | `publish =` |[m
[32m+[m[32m|---------------------|-------------------------|---------------------|----------------------------|-------------|[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-otel`        | 0.1.0                   | **N/A — not published** | 15                       | `true` (declared, never published) |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-port-adapter`| 0.1.0                   | **N/A — not published** | 0 (substrate; source-only) | default `true`, never published |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-errors`      | 0.1.0                   | **N/A — not published** | 3                        | default `true`, never published |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-context`     | 0.1.0                   | **N/A — not published** | 0 (FocalPoint workspace member only) | `false` |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-config`      | 0.1.0                   | **N/A — not published** | 2                        | `false` |[m
[32m+[m[32m| `pheno-cli-base`    | 0.1.0                   | **N/A — not published** | 3                        | `false` |[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m**Headline finding:** All 6 crates are path-only monorepo deps. **Zero are published to crates.io.** No SemVer pinning exists anywhere in the fleet — every consumer uses `path = "..."` or `workspace = true`. Therefore the "outdated dep" condition is structurally inapplicable; the audit dimension that was specified is empty.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m---[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m## Method[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Grep for fleet consumers[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mPattern: `^pheno-<name>\s*=\s*` over `**/Cargo.toml` (head_limit 300). Output captured in §"Per-crate details" below. Mirrors of source `Cargo.toml` (the `[package]` table that *declares* the crate, not consumes it) were filtered out via secondary search for `name = "pheno-<name>"`.[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Version-on-crates.io[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mPrimary: `cargo search --limit 1 pheno-<name>`. Sanity-check baseline (same command) returned real data for unrelated crates:[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m- `serde` → 1.0.228 ✓[m
[32m+[m[32m- `tokio` → 1.52.3 ✓[m
[32m+[m[32m- `opentelemetry` → 0.32.0 ✓[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mFor all 6 pheno-* crates, `cargo search` returned **zero bytes / exit 0** (suspicious), so I cross-verified with the crates.io REST API using a custom User-Agent (the default `curl` UA is rate-limited):[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m```[m
[32m+[m[32mcurl -H "User-Agent: dep-audit-cli/1.0" https://crates.io/api/v1/crates/<name>[m
[32m+[m[32m```[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mResult for all 6:[m
[32m+[m[32m```json[m
[32m+[m[32m{"errors":[{"detail":"crate `<name>` does not exist"}]}[m
[32m+[m[32m```[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m→ **Confirmed: none of the 6 are published.**[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32m### Source-declared version[m
[32m+[m
[32m+[m[32mRead each crate's primary `Cargo.toml` `[package]` table. All 6 declare `version = "0.1.0"`. Mirrors (e.g. `argis-extensions/pheno-otel/Cargo.toml`, `focalpoint-wt-v12-16-17/pheno-context/Cargo.toml`) also declare `0.1.0` — no drift between source and mirrors.[m
[32m+[m
